ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00
 1 Figure 10: eCPRI One-Way Delay Measurement procedure [2] 2 An O-RU that supports the eCPRI based delay measurement capability, shall be able to support simultaneous operation 3 of delay measurements over any processing element configured as described in section 4.5. For each processing element 4 configured for use by the delay measurement procedure, the O-RU shall keep a record of the number of responses, requests 5 and follow-up messages transmitted by the O-RU. 6
4.10 O-RU Monitoring of C/U Plane Connectivity  7 The O-RU is responsible for monitoring the C/U plane connection and raising an alarm if the logical C/U-plane connection 8 associated with a processing-element fails. The O-RU uses a timer to monitor the C/U plane connection on a per 9 processing-element basis. This timer is enabled only when at least one array-carrier using the processing-element is in 10 the active state and is reset whenever it receives any C/U plane data flows associated with the particular processing-11 element. Because of the variety of PHY and C/U plane configurations, the O-RU cannot independently determine the 12 minimum frequency of messages across the fronthaul interface. Therefore, as a default, the O-RU shall use a timer value 13 of 160 milliseconds for monitoing the C/U plane connection. An O-RU may indicate that its C/U-plane monitoring timer 14 is configurable, by the presence of the cu-plane-monitoring container in the o-ran-supervision.yang model. A 15 NETCONF client can use the container to configure the O-RU’s timer value, including being able to disable the operation 16 of C/U Plane monitoring. 17
Chapter 5 Software Management 18 The Software Management function provides a set of operations allowing the desired software build to be downloaded, 19 installed and activated at O-RU. Successful software activation operation does not mean an O-RU is running the just 20 activated software build. An O-RU reset RPC is required to trigger the O-RU to take the activated software build into 21 operational use. 22

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        39
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 A single software build is considered as set of internally consistent files compliant within such a build. Replacement of 1 files within a build is prohibited, as this will cause software version incompatibility. Software build is a subject of 2 versioning and maintenance and as such cannot be broken. 3 The use of compression and ciphering for the content of the software build is left to vendor implementation. The only file 4 which shall never be ciphered is the manifest.xml file.  5 It is also Vendor's responsibility to handle SW Build / package / file integrity check. 6 The O-RU provides a set of so called "software slots" or "slots". Each slot provides an independent storage location for a 7 single software build. The number of slots offered by O-RU depends on the device’s capabilities. At least two writable 8 slots shall be available at the O-RU for failsafe update operation. Presence of read only slot is optional. The software slots 9 are resources provided by the O-RU and as such are not the subject of creation and deletion. The size of individual 10 software slots is fixed and determined by the O-RU's vendor and sufficient to accommodate the full software build. 11 Note: procedures used in Software Management are covered by o-ran.software-management.yang module. 12
5.1 Software Package 13 The software package is delivered by the O-RU vendor. 14 Each software package includes: 15 - manifest.xml 16 - software files to be installed on O-RU 17  18 The name of package should follow the following format: 19 “<Vendor Code><Vendor Specific Field>[#NUMBER].EXT” 20 Where: 21 - Vendor Code is a mandatory part which has two capital characters, 22 - Vendor Specific Field is any set of characters allowed in filename. The value must not include character “_” 23 (underscore) or “#” (hash). The value can be defined per vendor for the human readable information. Version 24 information is necessary in the Vendor Specific Field which defines load version, 25 - NUMBER is optional and used when the original file is split into smaller pieces – number after “#” indicates the 26 number of a piece. Numbering starts from 1 and must be continuous, 27 - EXT is a mandatory part which defines the extension of filename. A vendor provides one or more software packages. 28 Each software package shall be compressed by zip. 29 Note: the name of package needs a <Vendor Code> prefix to avoid issue if two vendors provide files with same name. 30 Note: the NETCONF client shall support ZIP functionality to enable support of compressed files types.  31 Note: the operator needs to manage and control which O-RU files will be stored and used in the file server, e.g., based on 32 O-RU files provided by O-RU vendors and network configurations. The operator needs to make sure that only the 33 expected version of O-RU files will be transferred from the file server to the O-RU. Different versions of files for O-RU 34 with the same vendor and same product code should be avoided. 35 The content of the manifest.xml file allows to maintain software update process correctly in terms of compatibility 36 between O-RU hardware and software build to be downloaded. The content of the Manifest file prohibits the O-RU from 37 installing software builds designed for device based on different hardware. The format of the manifest.xml file is: 38 <xml> 39 <manifest version=”1.0”> /// @version describes version of file format (not the content) 40  <products> 41   <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x11” name=”RUXX.x11” build-Id=”1”/>  42   <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x12” name=”RUXX.x12” build-Id=”1”/> 43   <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818818\…” name=”RUYY” build-Id=”2”/>  44

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        40
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00   /// @vendor is as reported by O-RU 1   /// @code is a regular expression that is checked against productCode reported by O-RU 2   /// @name is optional and used for human reading – MUST NOT be used for other purposes! 3   /// @buildId is value of build@id (see below) 4  </products> 5  <builds> 6   <build id=”1” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 7   /// @id is index of available builds. 8   /// @bldName and @bldVersion are used in YANG (build-name, build-version) 9    <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 10 package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 11    <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 12 package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 13    /// @fileName and @fileVersion are used in YANG (name, version) 14    /// @path is full path (with name and extension) of a physical file, relative to 15 package root folder,used in YANG (local-path) 16    /// @checksum is used to chech file integrity on O-RU side 17   </build> 18   <build id=”2” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 19    <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 20 package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 21    <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 22 package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 23    <file fileName=”zzzz” fileVersion=”1.5” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 24 package -root-folder” checksum=”ABCDEF”/ > 25   </build> 26  </builds> 27 </manifest> 28 </xml> 29  30 Note: Keywords in manifest.xml example are in bold, the keywords must be strictly followed considering of cross-vendor 31 cases. 32 Note 2: Correspondency between content of manifest.xml tags and content of o-ran-software-management.yang is: 33 - XML tag "product vendor" corresponds to content leaf "vendor-code", 34 - XML tag "code" corresponds to content of leaf "product-code", 35 - XML tag "build-Id" corresponds to content of leaf "build-id", 36 - XML tag "bldName" corresponds to content of leaf "build-name", 37 - XML tag "bldVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "build-version", 38 - XML tag "fileName" corresponds to content of leaf "name" in list "files", 39 -XML tag "fileVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "version" in list "files" 40

 1  2 Figure 11: Inventory fetch call flow 3 Software Inventory is fetched by a NETCONF Client using the NETCONF get rpc filtered over the software-slot 4 container. The response contains information about each software slot and its contents. 5 The following information is provided by software-inventory reply message: 6 a) name - name of the software slot (the name is defined by the O-RU vendor) 7 b) status - status of the software package. Status of the package can be  8  - VALID - Slot contains a software build considered as proven valid. 9  - INVALID - software build is not currently used by O-RU. The software is considered by the O-RU as 10 damaged (e.g. wrong CRC). 11 Activation of a software slot containing an invalid software build shall be prohibited. Note: failed software install 12 operation can cause a slot status to change to "Invalid". 13  - EMPTY - software slot does not contain a software package. Activation of an empty software slot shall be 14 prohibited.  15 c) active - indicates if the software stored in particular slot is activated at the moment. 16  - True - software slot contains an activated software build. Active::True can be assigned only for slots with 17 status "Valid". At any time, only one slot in the O-RU MUST be marked as Active::True. The O-RU shall reject 18 activation for software slots with status "Empty" and "Invalid". 19  - False - software slot contains passive software build or is empty 20 d) running - informs if software stored in particular slot is used at the moment. 21

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        42
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00  - True - software slot contains the software build used by the O-RU in its current run. 1  - False - software slot contains a software build not used by O-RU at the moment. 2 e) access – informs about access rights for the current slot 3 - READ_ONLY – The slot is intended only for factory software, activation of such software slot means 4 performing a factory reset operation and a return to factory defaults settings. 5 - READ_WRITE – slot used for updating software 6 f) product-code - product code provided by the vendor, specific to the product. 7 g) vendor-code - unique code of the vendor. 8 h) build-id - Identity associated with the software build. This id is used to find the appropriate build-version for 9 the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 10 i) build-name - Name of the software build. 11 j) build-version - Version of the software build for the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 12 k) files – list of files in build 13 l) name – name of one particular file 14 m) version – version of the file 15 n) local-path - complete path of the file on local file system 16 o) integrity - result of the file integrity check 17 - OK – file integrity is correct 18 - NOK – file is corrupted 19 If a slot contains a file with integrity::NOK, the O-RU shall mark the whole slot with status::INVALID. The content of a 20 software-slot is fully under O-RU's management - including removal of the content occupying the slot (in case the slot is 21 subject of software update procedure), control of file system consistency and so on. The slot content shall not be removed 22 until there is a need for new software to be installed.  23 Note: The empty slot parameters shall be as follows 24 name: up to vendor, not empty 25 status: "INVALID" 26 active: False 27 running: False 28 access: READ_WRITE 29 product-code: up to vendor 30 vendor code: up to vendor 31 build-name: null (empty string) 32 build-version: null (empty string) 33 files: empty 34

O-RU restarts and performs 11 startup procedure as described in Chapter 3 as regular startup with new software version running.  12
5.6 Software update scenario 13 An example scenario of a successful software update procedure can be as follows: 14 1. NETCONF client performs a software inventory operation and determines that a new software package is 15 available and can be installed on the O-RU 16 2. NETCONF client using the software-download rpc requests the O-RU to download a software package (if the 17 software package contains several files, steps 2-4 need to be performed repeatedly until all files have been 18 downloaded) 19 3. O-RU sends rpc response that download was started 20 4. O-RU finishes downloading the file(s) and reports this by sending the download-event notification 21 5. NETCONF client requests installation of the software using software-install rpc, and provides the slot name 22 where the software needs to be installed along with a list of filenames to be installed (if the software package 23 contains only one file, the list will contain only one entry) 24 6. O-RU sends rpc response that installation was started 25 7. O-RU sets installation slot status to INVALID 26 8. O-RU installs the software and after successful installation (with checksum control) changes status of the slot to 27 VALID 28 9. O-RU notifies the NETCONF client that the installation is finished using install-event notification 29 10. NETCONF client requests the O-RU to activate the newly installed software using the software-activate rpc 30 11. O-RU sends rpc response that activation was started 31 12. For requested slot, O-RU changes active to True and at the same time sets activate to False on previously active 32 slot 33 13. O-RU notifies NETCONF client about activation finished using the activation-event notification 34 14. NETCONF client restarts the O-RU forcing it to use the newly installed and activated software into use. O-RU 35 restarts as regular startup with new software version running. 36

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        49
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00
5.7 Factory Reset  1 O-RU can be reset to the factory default software by activating the software-slot containing the factory default software 2 and initiating NETCONF reset rpc. O-RU may clear persistent memory data during factory reset as vendor 3 implementation option. 4  5

This state is optional. 14  15 [oper-state] 16 O-RU Controller is able to change oper-state defined in o-ran-hardware of the O-RU by using remote procedure call reset. 17 In this case, the O-RU responds <rpc-reply><ok> prior to reset operation. Whatever the previous state is, the O-RU oper-18 state starts from disabled when O-RU receives reset. 19

6.2 Framework for optional feature handling 17 This section describes the common and optional features about Configuration Management. 18 An O-RU may have some features which are not supported by other O-RUs, i.e. optional feature(s). In this case, the O-19 RU needs to inform the O-RU controller which features the O-RU can provide, and this can be achieved by exchanging 20 NETCONF capabilities. 21 Some of the YANG models are optional for the O-RU to support. For example, in this version of the management plane 22 specification, those models associated with External IO and Antenna Line Devices are not essential for the operation of 23 the O-RAN fronthaul interface. Other mandatory models define optional feature capabilities. 24

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        55
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 The NETCONF Server shall use the ietf-yang-library model (RFC 7895) [20] to list the namespace of the models 1 supported by the Server. If an O-RU/NETCONF server does not return the namespace associated with an optional YANG 2 model, the NETCONF client determines that the O-RU does not support the optional capability associated with the model. 3 In addition, for each supported schema, the ietf-yang-library lists the YANG feature names from this module that are 4 supported by the server. The details of optional models and features are defined in Annex C. 5
6.3 M-Plane Operational State 6 The o-ran-mplane-int YANG model allows the O-RU to report the connectivity to NETCONF clients on a per sub-7 interface level. The client information includes the IP address(es) for the client(s) as well as the link-layer address used 8 to forward packets towards the various management plane clients. 9
Chapter 7 Performance Management 10 This chapter provides the description of scenarios related to performance management. It consists of 2 functions. One is 11 for the measurement activation and the other is the collection of measurement results. 12 7.1 Measurement Activation and De-activation 13 The measurement activation at the start-up installation is also allowed as described in chapter 3.  14 Pre-condition:  15 M-Plane is operational.  16 Post-condition: 17 Measurement is activated or deactivated as per NETCONF client’s request. 18 This sub-section provides information about how to activate and de-activate the performance measurement via 19 NETCONF <edit-config> to O-RU. The performance measurement is defined as o-ran-performance-management YANG 20 module. In case of multiple NETCONF clients, only one NETCONF client shall activate/deactivate the measurements in 21 the O-RU. 22 In the performance-management YANG module, the following parameters are defined. 23 - group of the measurement results, e.g., transceiver-measurement-result and, rx-window-measurement-object. 24 - measurement-interval: measurement interval for the measurement-objects to measure the performance 25 periodically, e.g., 300, 600, 900 seconds. It is defined per the group of the measurement result. 26 - measurement-object: target metric to measure the performance, e.g., RX_POWER, TX_POWER, defined as key 27 parameter. 28 - active: enable/disable the performance measurement per measurement-object. This value is Boolean. Default is 29 FALSE. 30 - start-time and end-time: to report the time of measurement start and end for the measurement-object at each 31 measurement-interval. 32 - object-unit: unit to measure the performance per object, e.g., O-RU, physical port number, antenna, carrier. The 33 object-unit may be configurable Identifier object-unit-id means e.g., physical port number when object unit set 34 to physical port number. 35 - report-info: the reporting info to the measurement-object, e.g., MAXIMUM, MINIMUM, FIRST, LATEST, 36 FREQUENCY_TABLE and COUNT. Multiple info can be considered for one object if necessary. 37 - Optional configurable parameter(s) for report-info: some configurable parameters to report, e.g., function, bin-38 count, upper-bound, lower-bound. For the bin-count configuration, it shall be less than the parameter max-bin-39 count that is the capability information of NETCONF server for the maximum configurable value for bin-count. 40 - Additional reporting information for report-info: some additional information to report info, e.g., date-and-time. 41  42

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        56
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 The detail of the parameters per measurement-object and the group of measurement result are defined in Annex B. 1 The measurement-interval of measurement-object may be set to common or different values per group of the 2 measurement result.  3 It is allowed that the measurement is activated and deactivated at any time. When different parameter measurements have 4 intervals with a common factor, the O-RU shall synchronize the boundary of these measurements aligned with this factor, 5 irrespective of when the different measurements are activated. And all of start points of the measurement-intervals shall 6 be synchronized to zero o’clock mid-night by using an equation {full seconds (hour, minute and second) modulo 7 ‘measurement-interval’ = 0}, in order to ensure the same start and end of the measurement-intervals between O-RUs. 8 For more detail see the following illustration. 9
 10 Figure 25: synchronization of measurement-interval. 11  12 The modification of the configurable parameters for the measurement shall be allowed while active for the corresponding 13 measurement-object is set to FALSE. 14 All of the measurements are optionally supported in the O-RU.  15 The report-info, e.g., count, shall be started from 0 at the boundary of every measurement-interval. No accumulation 16 is applied between the measurement-intervals. 17  7.2 Collection and Reporting of Measurement Result 18 This sub-section provides the description of scenarios used to collect measurement results. There are two options. 19 - NETCONF process: Create-subscription from NETCONF client and NETCONF notification from NETCONF server 20 are used.  21 - File Management process: File upload mechanism is used for the measurement file from O-RU to configured file 22 server(s) that O-RU can reach to. 23 Both methods are mandatory for the O-RU. The method(s) to be used is the matter of NETCONF client. 24 In case of multiple NETCONF clients, the O-RU shall report the same notification-based measurement results to all 25 subscribed NETCONF clients, and the O-RU shall upload file-based results to all configured fileservers. 26 7.2.1 NETCONF process 27 This process needs the NETCONF capability: urn:ietf:params:netconf:capability:notification:1.0 28 1. NETCONF client subscribes to one or more measurement group(s) and/or measurement-object(s) to collect the 29 measurement result by sending NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to NETCONF server in the O-RU. In this 30

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        57
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 message, startTime and stopTime for the notification may be configurable. NETCONF client can configure the 1 notification-interval in the performance-measurement YANG module.  2 2.  NETCONF server sends NETCONF notification messages periodically to the client as configured by the notification-3 interval. The NETCONF notification message contains subscribed measurement group(s) and/or measurement-4 object(s). The notification-interval doesn’t need to be same as the measurement-interval. The notification timing 5 different from the measurement-interval is a matter to O-RU implementation. 6 This procedure is described in the following figure. 7

In order to subscribe 10 multiple notifications, the appropriate create-subscription message is required. Please refer to setion 8.2 for the 11 appropriate example of create-subscription of multiple notifications. 12 In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall send <close-session> operation from the subscription 13 session. If NETCONF session is terminated by <kill-session>, the subscribed notification is terminated as well.  14 This procedure is described in the following figure. 15

 1 Figure 27: NETCONF process of Measurement Result Collection to end 2 When notification-interval is larger than measurement-interval, one notification may contain multiple stats which have 3 consecutive periods indicating start-time and end-time for the measurement. 4 When notification-interval is smaller than measurement-interval, one notification may not contain the stats which 5 start-time and end-time are not applicable to the period for the notification. 6 For example, when notification-interval = 60min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 7 measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains 2 measurement results for 8 measurement-object#A with consecutive start-time and end-time, and 4 measurement results for measurement-9 object#B with consecutive start-time and end-time.  10 For the other example, when notification-interval = 15min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min 11 and measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains one measurement results for 12 measurement-object#B but not for measurement-object#A. next notification contains both measurements result for 13 measurement-object#A and #B. 14  15 7.2.2 File Management process 16 NETCONF client needs to configure a parameter of performance measurement YANG module ‘enable-SFTP-upload’ 17 to enable or disable the periodic file upload mechanism via NETCONF <edit-config>. Its default is FALSE. 18 In addition, the performance measurement YANG module defines file-upload-interval, remote-SFTP-upload-path, 19 credentials information of the file server and enable-random-file-upload as configurable parameters. 20 Following types of authentications are supported for performance file upload: 21 a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 22 b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 23 When the parameter enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE, O-RU shall store the performance measurement files in the 24 generic folder in O-RU, i.e., O-RAN/PM/. Every file-upload-interval, O-RU pushes the latest file to upload to the 25 remote-SFTP-upload-path of the configured SFTP servers if enable-SFTP-upload is set to TRUE. Otherwise, the 26 performance measurement file is not created and uploaded. The number of maximum performance files to be stored in 27 O-RU simultaneously is a matter for O-RU implementation. The O-RU shall manage its own storage space by deleting 28 the older files autonomously.  29

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        59
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 The O-RU shall ensure that the start-time and the end-time within the name of the performance measurement file are 1 synchronized with the same manner as measurement-interval by using file-upload-interval. 2 If the parameter enable-random-file-upload is set to TRUE, the O-RU shall randomize the timing to upload SFTP file 3 after the performance measurement file is ready to upload. The randomized timing is an O-RU implementation matter 4 and shall not be later than next file-upload-interval. 5 The file name of the performance measurement is: 6 C<start-time>_<end-time>_<name>.csv 7 - Starting with a capital letter “C”. 8 - Format of <start-time> and <end-time> can be local time or UTC. 9 Local time format is YYYYMMDDHHMM+HHMM, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute, timezone “+” or 10 “-“, hour and minute for the time zone. 11 UTC format is YYYYMMDDHHMMZ, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute and with a special UTC 12 designator ("Z")   13 Time zone offset is provided by timezone-utc-offset in o-ran-operation.yang. 14 - <name> in ietf-hardware is used  15 - “_” underscore is located between <start-time>, <end-time> and <name> 16 - File extension is “csv” as csv format file. 17 Example of measurement file is: 18 C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv. 19  20 The file format of the performance measurement has following rule: 21 1. Each line starts with the measurement-object identifier, which measurement can be switched to TRUE or FALSE 22 by active parameter. The identifier of each measurement-object is defined in Annex B. 23 2. After the measurement-object identifier, the name of measurement-object, start-time, end-time are followed. 24 3. Since the report-info results of any measurement-object are measured per object-unit, object-unit-id and set of 25 report-info are repeated in one line. 26 4. When multiple report-info parameters exist per object-unit, all of the report-info are consecutively listed until the 27 next object-unit-id. The order of parameters, such as object-unit-id, report-info and additional information for the 28 report-info, shall be same as the order of those listed in NETCONF notification defined in o-ran-performance-29 management YANG module. 30 Example of measurement result in one line is: 31 1, RX_ON_TIME, 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00, 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00, 0, 123, AAAA, 1, 123, BBBB, 2, 123, CCCC, 3, 32 123, DDDD 33 - Measurement-object-identifier: 1 34 - Name of measurement-object: RX_ON_TIME 35 - start-time: 2018-05-18T13:00:00+09:00 as measurement start-time. 36 - end-time: 2018-05-18T13:30:00+09:00 as measurement end-time 37 - EAXC_ID: 0 38 - Count for EAXC_ID#0 : 123 39 - name of transport-flow information:  AAAA 40

Chapter 8 Fault Management 35 Fault management is responsible for sending alarm notifications to the NETCONF Client. FM contains Fault Management 36 Managed Element and via this Managed Element alarm notifications can be disabled or enabled. 37 The NETCONF Server is responsible for managing an “active-alarm-list”. Alarms with severity “warning” are excluded 38 from this list. When an alarm is detected it is added to the list; when the alarm reason disappears then the alarm is cleared 39 - removed from the “active-alarm-list”. Furthermore, when the element that was the “fault-source” of an alarm is deleted 40 then all related alarms are removed from the “active-alarm-list”. 41 The NETCONF Client can read “active-alarm-list” by get rpc operation. 42

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        61
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00
 1 Figure 28: Read Active Alarms 2
8.1 Alarm Notification 3 The NETCONF Server is responsible to send <alarm-notif> to a NETCONF Client when the NETCONF Client has 4 “subscribed” to alarm notification and: 5 - a new alarm is detected (this can be the same alarm as an already existing one, but reported against a different “fault-6 source” than the existing alarm)  7 - an alarm is removed from the list   8 Removal of alarms from the list due to deletion of “fault-source” element is considered as clearing and cause sending of 9 <alarm-notif> to the NETCONF Client. This applies to alarms which were explicitly related to the deleted “fault-source” 10 element. The rationale for such is to avoid misalignment between NETCONF Clients when one NETCONF Client deletes 11 an element.  12 NETCONF Server reports in <alarm-notif> only for new active or cancelled alarms, not all active alarms. 13

ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00

8.3 Fault Sources 3 Alarm notifications reported by NETCONF Server contain element “fault-source” which indicates the origin of an alarm. 4 In general values of “fault-source” are based on names defined as YANG leafs: 5 - Source (Examples: fan, module, PA, port) 6 indicates that origin of the alarm within the O-RU. Value of “fault-source” is based on element name. 7 Note: In case the NETCONF Server reports an unknown “fault-source”, the NETCONF Client can discard the 8 <alarm-notif>. 9 - Source (other than when an element is within the O-RU) 10 Value of fault-source may be empty or may identify the most likely external candidate; for example, antenna line.   11  12 Alarms with different “fault-id”, “fault-source” or "fault-severity" are independent: 13 - Multiple alarms with same “fault-id” may be reported with different “fault-source”.  14 - Multiple alarms with same “fault-source” may be reported with different “fault-id”.  15 - When an alarm with a "fault-id" and a "fault-source" is reported with a "fault-severity" and its severity of alarm 16 condition is upgraded or degraded, NETCONF server reports a new alarm with the same "fault-id" and the same "fault-17 source" with the updgraded or degraded "fault-severity" with "is-cleared"::FALSE and clears the previous alarm with 18 the report of the "fault-id", "fault-source" and "fault-severity" with "is-cleard":: TRUE.  19 The range of "fault-id" is separated to common and vendor specific. The common fault-ids are defined in Annex A and 20 more number will be used in future. The vendor specific range for the fault-id shall be [1000 .. 65535]. 21 Alarm notifications reported by the NETCONF Server contain names of the “affected-objects” which indicate elements 22 affected by the fault. In case the origin of the alarm is within the O-RU, other elements than “fault-source” which will not 23 work correctly due to the alarm are reported via “affected-objects”. In case the origin of the fault is outside of the O-RU, 24 the O-RU elements which will not work correctly due to the fault are reported via “affected-objects”. 25

ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00
Chapter 9 File Management 1 This chapter specifies File Management for the O-RU. Following operations are supported as a File Management. 2 - upload (see subsection 9.2) 3  File upload from O-RU to O-DU/NMS triggered by O-DU/NMS. 4 - retrieve file list (see subsection 9.3) 5  O-DU/NMS retrieves the file list in O-RU. 6 - download (see subection 9.4) 7  File download from O-DU/NMS to O-RU triggered by O-DU/NMS 8 Note: file-download has different purpose with software-download specified in subsection 5.3. For example, file-9 download can be used for Beamforming configuration in subsection 12.4. 10 File transfers are done with sFTP. Following types of authentications are supported for file management: 11 a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 12 b) Certificate for both RU and sFTP server authentication 13 Following other sections are related with File Management. 14 - Subsection 7.2.2: File Management process (can be used for on demand file upload purpose, since subsection 7.2.2 15 covers periodic file upload) 16 - Subsection 11.2: Log Management 17 - Subsection 12.4: Beamforming Configuration 18
9.1 File System Structure 19 The file System structure of the O-RU is represented as a logical structure that is used by the file management procedures 20 defined in the rest of this chapter. If the O-RU’s physical file structure differs from the logical file structure defined below, 21 the O-RU is responsible for performing the mapping between the two structures. 22 The O-RU shall support the standardized logical folders. In this version of the M-Plane specification, the following 23 standardized folders are defined: 24 O-RAN/log/ 25 O-RAN/PM/ 26 O-RAN/transceiver/ 27 And for those O-RU’s supporting beamforming 28 O-RAN/beamforming/ 29 The O-RU may additionally support vendor defined folders which are out of scope of this specification. 30

The behaviour of O-DU/NMS is out 1 of scope when O-DU/NMS receives failure notification from the O-RU. 2 Following rpc is used for upload operation. 3 -rpc: file-upload 4 -  input 5 -  local-logical-file-path: the logical path of file to be uploaded (no wildcard is allowed) 6 -  remote-file-path: URI of file on the O-DU/NMS 7 -  output 8 -  status: whether O-RU accepted or rejected the upload request  9 -  reject-reason: the human readable reason why O-RU rejects the request (only applicable if status is rejected) 10 In the rpc-reply, status whether the O-RU receives the upload request or rejects due to some reason (e.g., the number of 11 limitation to upload simultaneously) is replied. Chapter 10 Synchronization Aspects 1 This chapter provides the Management Plane’s interactions with various aspects of the time synchronization of the O-2 RU. In general, the O-RU is responsible for managing its synchronization status, to select one or more synchronization 3 input source(s) (based on vendor specific implementation) and assure that the resulting accuracy meets that required by 4 the Radio Access Technology being implemented. 5
10.1 Sync Status Object 6 This sync container provides synchronization state of the module. If the O-DU is interested in Sync status, it may send 7 NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to the NETCONF Server in the O-RU.  Event notifications will be sent whenever 8 the state of the O-RU synchronization changes. 9 The State of O-RU synchronization is indicated by the following allowed values: 10 - LOCKED: O-RU is in the locked mode, as defined in ITU-T G.810.  11 - HOLDOVER: O-RU clock is in holdover mode. 12 - FREERUN: O-RU clock isn’t locked to an input reference and is not in the holdover mode. 13 The sync container allows the O-RU to list via an array the synchronization sources which it is capable of supporting.   14 The allowed values are: 15 • GNSS 16 • PTP 17 • SYNCE 18
10.2 Sync Capability Object 19 The module’s synchronization capability is provided via this object.  This indicates the accuracy of the derived Telecom 20 Slave Clock (T-TSC) to which the module’s design is capable of. For details on the actual capability levels, see section 21 9.3 of the O-RAN WG4 CUS plane specification [2]. There are two enumerations possible: 22 • CLASS_B 23 • ENHANCED 24
10.3 PTP Configuration 25 This container defines the configuration of Precision Time Protocol.   26 domain-number 27 This parameter indicates the Domain Number for PTP announce messages. Allowed values: 0 ~ 255. 28 Default: 24. 29 Note: ITU-T G.8275.1 [22] uses domain numbers in the range 24...43, but the entire range is allowed to ensure 30 flexibility of the M-Plane specification. For ITU-T G.8275.2 domain numbers from range 44…63 shall be used. 31 accepted-clock-classes 32 Contains the list of PTP acceptable Clock Classes, sorted in the descending order. 33 Note: The sender must generate the list of acceptable clock classes. The list must be sorted in descending order. Each 34 accepted Clock Class value must appear only once in the list. Depending on implementation, the receiver may interpret 35 the list in either of two ways: 36

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        70
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 a) use only the first (i.e. the maximum) item in the list, interpreting it as a threshold value for acceptable clock 1 classes, while ignoring all other items in the list; 2 b) use the whole list, interpreting it as an explicit list of acceptable clock classes. 3 Default: 7, 6 4 clock-class 5 The PTP Clock Class accepted by the O-RU. Allowed values: 0 ~ 255. 6 Note: Not all values are compliant to [22], but the entire range is allowed in M-plane specification to ensure flexibility. 7 The values can be validated/filtered on the receiver side, if necessary. 8 ptp-profile 9 Defines which PTP profile will be used. 10 Allowed values: 11 • G_8275_1 (multicast over Ethernet will be used, see: ITU-T G.8275.1) 12 • G_8275_2 (unicast over IP will be used, see: ITU-T G.8275.2) 13 Default: G_8275_1. 14 delay-asymmetry 15 Defines the static phase error in the recovered PTP timing signal to be compensated at the O-DU. The error is defined in 16 units of nanoseconds in the range ±10 000 ns. According to ITU-T G.810 [23] and IEEE1588v2-2008 [24] the sign of the 17 parameter is interpreted as follows: 18 • If the phase error to be compensated is negative, then the recovered timing signal shall be advanced by the time 19 interval equal to the configured value to compensate the error. 20 • If the phase error to be compensated is positive, then the recovered timing signal shall be delayed by the time 21 interval equal to the configured value to compensate the error. 22 Default: 0 23 Note: Modification of this parameter may have impact on RF transmission, but shall occur without unit restart. 24 Note: This parameter is optional for support. If the O-RU does not support this value, the O-RU uses the default value. If 25 the O-RU does not support manual compensation, it ignores the parameter setting. 26 Note: Granularity of the applied value depends on the architecture and implementation of the system clock, and therefore, 27 may vary across vendors. 28 10.3.1 G.8275.1 specific parameters 29 multicast-mac -address 30 The parameter defines the destination MAC address, used by the O-RU in the egress PTP messages. 31 Allowed values: 32 • FORWARDABLE (means that PTP shall use 01-1B-19-00-00-00  destination MAC address) 33 • NONFORWARDABLE (means that PTP shall use 01-80-C2-00-00-0E  destination MAC address) 34 Default value: FORWARDABLE. 35 10.3.2 G.8275.2 specific parameters 36 This section contains G.8275.2 specific parameters 37

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        71
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 local-ip-port 1 The parameter defines local ip address which will be used as a slave port for receiving ptp signal 2 master-ip-configuration 3 The parameter defines list of ip configuration of devices acting as ptp signal source. 4 local-priority 5 The parameter defines local priority or underlying master IP address. 6 ip-address 7 the parameter defines master IP address. 8 log-inter-sync-period 9 The parameter defines number of sync message during 1 second 10 Allowed values: 0 ~ -7 (this represents the value from 1 message per second to 128 messages per second) 11 log-inter-announce-period 12 The parameter defines number of announce message during 1 second 13 Allowed values: 0 ~ -3 (this represents the value from 1 message per second to 8 messages per second) 14  15
10.4 PTP Status 16 The PTP Status container is used to collect operational status information of the PTP ordinary clock, controlled by the O-17 RU. The object may be used to display operational information, which facilitates troubleshooting, to the operator. The 18 information in the object shall not be used by the O-DU to autonomously alter its operation. If the O-DU is interested in 19 PTP status, it may NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to the NETCONF Server in the O-RU. Notifications will only 20 indicate changes to the lock-state.  Before requesting or subscribing to PTP status information, the O-DU shall ensure 21 that PTP is supported by the O-RU by requesting the supported-timing-reference-types, as defined in this chapter 22 (Section 10.1). The following list includes the related parameters of this container. 23 reporting-period 24 This parameter defines minimum period in seconds between reports, sent by the NETCONF Server, for parameters in this 25 container. 26 default: 10 27 lock-state 28 This parameter indicates whether the integrated ordinary clock is synchronizing to the reference, recovered from PTP 29 flow. The exact definition when to indicate locked or unlocked is up to specific implementation. 30 • LOCKED: The integrated ordinary clock is synchronizing to the reference, recovered from PTP flow. 31 • UNLOCKED: The integrated ordinary clock is not synchronizing to the reference, recovered from PTP flow. 32 clock-class 33 This parameter contains the clock class of the clock, controlled by the O-RU. 34 sources 35 This parameter contains characteristics of PTP sources of the clock, controlled by the O-RU. 36 state 37

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        72
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 This parameter indicates status of the PTP source: 1 • PARENT: Indicates that the PTP signal from this source is currently used as a synchronization reference. 2 • OK: Indicates that the PTP signal from this source can be potentially used as a synchronization reference, i.e. 3 SSM messages, received from this source, contain acceptable clock quality level. 4 • NOK: Indicates that the PTP signal from this source cannot be used as a synchronization reference, i.e. SSM 5 messages, received from this source, contain unacceptable clock quality level. 6 • DISABLED: Indicates that SSMs are not received from this SyncE source. 7 See the related o-ran-sync YANG Model for the full details. 8
10.5 SyncE Configuration 9 This container defines the configuration of SyncE 10 acceptance-list-of-ssm 11 The parameter contains the list of SyncE acceptable Synchronization Status Messages (SSM). 12 Allowed values: 13 • PRC (Primary Reference Clock) 14 • PRS (Primary Reference Source-Stratum 1) 15 • SSU_A (Synchronisation Supply Unit A) 16 • SSU_B (Synchronisation Supply Unit B) 17 • ST2 (Stratum 2) 18 • ST3 (Stratum 3) 19 • ST3E (Stratum 3E) 20 • EEC1 (Ethernet Equipment Clock 1) 21 • EEC2 (Ethernet Equipment Clock 2) 22 • DNU (Do Not Use) 23 • NONE 24 ssm-timeout 25 The parameter contains the value of maximum duration in seconds for which the actual SSM value may be different 26 than configured values. 27

Chapter 11 Operations Use Cases 1
11.1 Supervision Failure 2 Section 3.6 describes the procedure by which an O-RU uses the expiry of a supervision watchdog timer to trigger 3 “supervision failure” condition. 4 Note, an O-RU operating in supervision failure may still have NETCONF sessions established with one or more 5 NETCONF clients with non-“sudo” privileges.  6 An O-RU that detects a supervision failure shall immediately cease RF transmission. The O-RU shall perform an 7 autonomous recovery reset procedure. This procedure will trigger the re-initialization of the transport layer and re-8 commencement of the start-up installation procedures defined in section 3. 9
11.2 Log management 10 There are two type of log managements, troubleshooting log and trace log. They are independent each other. 11 Troubleshooting log file contains the logs continuously collected before <start-troubleshooting-logs> rpc. Any logs 12 collected after <start-troubleshooting-logs> rpc are not contained. 13 Trace log file contains the logs continuously collected after <start-trace-logs> rpc. Any logs collected before <start-trace-14 logs> rpc are not contained. 15 11.2.1 Troubleshooting 16 By requesting technical logs an O-RU controller is able to get collected log data files that can be used for troubleshooting 17 purposes.  18 The O-RU provides all possible troubleshooting log files. The contents and log formats are dependent on O-RU 19 implementation. 20 The number and size of files provided by O-RU is not restricted but the O-RU may keep the number and size of files 21 reasonably small to allow completion of the whole “Troubleshooting data upload” scenario (all files) within 15 minutes 22 (with target to complete within 3 minutes). It is also recommended to provide more useful files first.  23 Note, the O-RU controller is free to continue the scenario till completion past the allowed time or skip requesting further 24 files. 25 The files should be compressed with compression method indicated by file name extension:  26  .gz (DEFLATE),  27  .lz4 (LZ4),  28  .xz (LZMA2 - xz utils),  29  .zip (DEFLATE - zlib library). 30 O-RU shall start collecting the troubleshooting logs.  31 The rpc <start-troubleshooting-logs> triggers the O-RU to start creating files containing troubleshooting logs. Completed 32 generation of files is indicated by NETCONF server to NETCONF client in form of a notification. 33

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        76
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00

 1 Figure 39: Overall Trace Log behaviour 2  3 11.3 Operational aspects of Antenna Line Devices 4 An O-RU can connect to one or more external equipment such as a RET, MultiRET, MHA, RAE and etc. 5 For the communication with the external equipment, AISG 2.0 protocol [26] as Layer 7 application and HDLC protocol 6 as Layer 2 data link are used. 7 - HDLC protocol is standardized by ISO/IEC 13239 (https://www.iso.org/standard/37010.html). Detailed information 8 can also be found in TS 25.462 [27]. 9 - AISG 2.0 protocol is standardized by “Control interface for antenna line devices Standard No. AISG v2.0” [26] which 10 is an adaptation of Iuant interface application layer defined in TS 25.466 [28] and formerly in TS 25.463 [29].  11 An O-RU may provide one or more ALD ports supporting connection with Antenna Line Devices. Each ALD port shall 12 be able to support more than one ALD (i.e., a chained ALD configuration). 13

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        80
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 This section describes the communication mechanisms based on AISG 2.0 protocol [26]. For communication with 1 external equipment, AISG 2.0 uses Application Part protocols (RETAP, TMAAP etc.) at Layer 7 and HDLC as a Layer 2 2 datalink protocol. 3 Note, further definitions of O-RU support for Antenna Line Devices will be included in a future version of this 4 specification, and will target support of the AISG 3.0 protocol. 5 11.3.1 HDLC Interworking 6 HDLC protocol is standardized by ISO/IEC 13239. Detailed information can also be found in TS 25.462 [27]. The AISG 7 2.0 protocol is standardized by “Control interface for antenna line devices Standard No. AISG v2.0” which is an 8 adaptation of Iuant interface application layer defined in TS 25.466 [28] and formerly in TS 25.463 [29]. 9 Note: the assumed HDLC communication speed is 9600 bits per second. 10 In order to handle collision detection in the HDLC branch, an O-RU supporting the ALD functionality shall support the 11 following running counters reported using the corresponding YANG model: 12 -  Frames with wrong FCS 13 -  Frames without stop flag 14 -  Number of received octets 15 For running counters served by the O-RU, both the O-RU and NETCONF Client shall handle wrap-over mechanism in a 16 way, that wrap over zero is not considered as erroneous situation. 17 A NETCONF client can recover these counters. From the changes observed in above counters, a NETCONF Client can 18 deduce the presence of a collision on the HDLC bus. Additional diagnostic information may be derived from how these 19 counters are incrementing. 20 Additionally, the O-RU implements "RPC Status" to indicate status of last "ald-communication" RPC to requestor. 21 -  Status - flow control indicator of last requested operation (Status of RPC). 22 Prior to any communication with ALD(s), the O-RU shall provide ALDs with DC power. The way of how DC power is 23 managed is out of scope of this interface specification. 24 In order to support collision detection and flow control, the following reference architecture with functional split is 25 defined: 26  27
28 Figure 40: ALD Reference Architecture 29 The result of the above architecture is, that below mentioned parts of HDLC message are processed by entities as 30 illustrated in Figure 41: 31

 1 Figure 41: Component's responsibility split. 2  3 11.3.2 ALD Operations 4 The NETCONF Client sends RPC <ald-communication> to the O-RU. The RPC has following input parameters: 5 - leaf: ald-port-id (uint8) - contains the identity of the ALD port. The O-RU shall output the data to (corresponds to O-6 RU resources provided to NETCONF Client as inventory information) 7 - leaf: ald-req-msg (up to 1200 bytes) - may contain HDLC address, control bits and payload (see: TS 25.462 for 8 details) 9 The O-RU performs HDLC communication with the ALD as follows: immediately after the requested payload is sent to 10 the ALD over the desired ALD port, the O-RU switches the ALD port into reception mode.  11 Note, for details of HDLC transmission and reception algorithm, please see TS 25.462, chapter 4.5 "Message timing". 12 Bits received within reception window are formed to octets and inserted as payload into ald-resp-msg. 13 The O-RU responds to the NETCONF Client using the <rpc-reply> message containing following parameters: 14 - leaf: ald-port-id (uint8) 15 - leaf: status 16 - leaf: ald-resp-msg (up to 1200 bytes) 17 - leaf: frames-with-wrong-crc (4 bytes) 18 - leaf: frames-without-stop-flag (4 bytes) 19 - leaf: number-of-received-octets (4 bytes) 20 Note: In case there is no response from the ALD received within the reception window, the record "ald-resp-msg" in 21 <rpc-reply> sent by the O-RU shall be empty. 22 After reception, the O-RU shall wait an additional 3ms before the next transmission towards HDLC bus is initiated. See 23 TS 25.462, chapter 4.5 "Message timing" for details. 24  25

11.4 Operational aspects of external IO 3 An O-RU can connect to one or more input and output ports for external device supervision and control. 4 The External IO has the following functions 5 - INPUT: Supervising external devices 6 - OUTPUT: Controlling external devices 7 Also external IO function include signalling to get the O-RU and O-RU controller in sync, enables port monitoring on 8 the O-RU and provides notification from the O-RU to an O-RU controller, and provides control from an O-RU controller 9 to the O-RU and enables output port controlling on the O-RU.  10 The O-RU only implements external IO yang module if the O-RU supports External IO aspect. 11 A change in condition of the external IO shall not affect other O-RU services such as RF transmission / reception 12 behaviour. 13 11.4.1 External input 14 This section explains single external input line case. For multiple external inputs case, same behaviour for each input shall 15 be processed individually. 16 For input, the O-RU and O-RU controller shall support two scenarios.  17 [1] To retrieve input state from O-RU controller and respond the input state from the O-RU to O-RU controller. 18 [2] To send notification from the O-RU to O-RU controller when input state is changed. 19 The value shall be 20  TRUE: Circuit is open. 21  FALSE: Circuit is closed 22 When nothing is connected to the line the value shall be TRUE. 23

12.2 User plane message routing 7 The purpose of U-Plane configuration is to define the relationship between U-Plane application endpoints in the O-DU 8 and those in the O-RU. After such relationships are defined, the application endpoints are able to exchange IQ data using 9 the U-Plane application protocol defined in [2]. 10 Precondition: 11 • M-Plane connectivity is established between NETCONF Client and NETCONF Server 12 12.2.1 Configurable format for eAxC_ID  13 The eAxC_ID is used by C/U-plane application to manage eCPRI communication between desired C/U-Plane application 14 components in O-DU and O-RU. 15 As defined in [2], the eAxC_ID consists of four parameters: DU-PORT, RU-PORT, CC-ID and BAND-SECTOR-ID. 16 Order of parameters in eAxC_ID must follow definitions in CUS-Plane spec. In this version of the O-RAN WG4 17 specification, the length of eAxC_ID is constant and equal to 16 bits. To enable optimal sharing of the 16 bits between 18 these four parameters, the assignment of eAxC_ID bits to parameters is not fixed. As a consequence, there is a need for 19 NETCONF client to configure the bit assignment to parameters mappings using the M-Plane interface. 20 To handle flexible bit assignment, configurable bitmasks are defined for each parameter.  21 Note: flexible configuration means, that bits of eAxC_ID can be assigned to parameters in runtime.  22 Rules to be followed by NETCONF Client when configuring bit assignments: 23 - notation used for parameters forming eAxC_ID is from the LSB. 24 - each parameter uses consecutive bits 25 - each parameter can occupy 0-16 bits 26 - single bit of eAxC_ID cannot be assigned to more than one parameter 27  28 RPC edit-config shall be used to configure bit assignments to O-RU. 29 Bit assignment change for parameters related to an existing carrier is not allowed. (Impacted carriers need to be 30 deactivated and deleted prior to any change in eAxC_ID configuration, and then be subsequently created and activated.) 31 An example of bit assignment usage where 3 bits are assigned to the BAND-SECTOR-ID, 3 bits for CC-ID, 1 bit for DU-32 PORT-ID and 3 bits for RU-PORT-ID is shown below: 33 <du-port-bitmask> 1111111000000000 </du-port-bitmask> 34 <band-sector-bitmask> 0000000111000000 </band-sector-bitmask> 35 <ccid-bitmask> 0000000000111000 </ccid-bitmask> 36 <ru-port-bitmask> 0000000000000111 </ru-port-bitmask> 37

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        88
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00
12.2.2 U-Plane endpoint addressing 1 Parameter “eaxc-id” for low-level-tx-endpoint and low-level-rx-endpoint, defined using an unsigned 16 bit integer, shall 2 follow the eAxC_ID addressing schema defined in section 12.2.1.  3 The NETCONF Client is responsible for assigning unique values to "eaxc_id" addresses of all low-level-rx-endpoint 4 elements and low-level-tx-endpoint elements, that are linked to the same interface element and are referenced by low-5 level-rx-link or/ low-level-tx-link respectively. Note: The same eAxC_id can be assigned to low-level-rx-endpoint and 6 low-level-tx-endpoint. 7 The NETCONF Server shall reject configuration requests violating the above-mentioned rules. 8 The default value of the "eaxc-id" parameters is zero. 9 12.2.3 General configuration scenario 10 Below is described the general scenario to be followed by a NETCONF Client in order to properly configure 11 communication between C/U-Plane endpoints in the O-DU and O-RU. 12 All operations can be performed in any order (including combining some of them in one request) provided assumed result 13 (overall configuration) of each request sent by NETCONF Client is valid. Note selected highlighted rules below: 14 -  eaxc-id is unique for all endpoints linked with same interface element and linked with any low-level-rx-link or low-15 level-tx-link element 16 -  at the moment of creation, every low-level-rx-link must be linked to an existing rx-array-carrier element and existing 17 processing-element element  18 -  at the moment of creation, every low-level-tx-link must be linked to an existing tx-array-carrier element and existing 19 processing-element element 20 1) NETCONF Client determines the presence of following elements offered by NETCONF Server: 21 - tx-arrays  - by fetching the list of tx-arrays in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 22 - rx-arrays - by fetching the list of rx-arrays in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 23 - low-level-tx-endpoint elements - by fetching the list static-low-level-tx-endpoints in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 24 - low-level-rx-endpoint elements - by fetching the list static-low-level-rx-endpoints in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 25 - interface elements - by fetching list of interfaces in o-ran-interfaces.yang 26 2) NETCONF Client determines capabilities exposed by static-low-level-tx-and points and static-low-level-rx-endpoints. 27 Additionally. NETCONF Client determines capabilities exposed by "endpoint-types" and "endpoint-capacity-sharing-28 groups" and specific parameters proprietary to [tr]x-array(s). Obtained information must be respected when NETCONF 29 Client configures low-level-[tr]x-endpoints refferenced to static-low-level[tr]x-endpoints by parameter "name". 30 3) For elements determined in step 1) NETCONF Client examines relationship between  31 - static-low-level-tx-endpoint elements and tx-array elements in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 32 - static-low-level-rx-endpoint elements and rx-array elements in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 33 - static-low-level-tx-endpoint elements and interface elements 34 - static-low-level-rx-endpoint elements and interface elements 35 - tx-arrays, rx-arrays and their elements in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang. 36 Note: Netconf Client retrievies the content of o-ran-beamforming,yang module to obtain knowledge regarding 37 beamforming-related parameters that apply for particular Netconf Server. This step is optional, as o-ran-38 beamforming.yang module exists only in case Netconf Server supports beamforming. Obtained parameters are needed by 39 Netconf Client to perform beamforming control. 40 4) For every static-low-level-rx-endpoint NETCONF Client determines endpoint's ability to support non-time managed 41 and/or time managed traffic.  Information about delayed traffic type supported by endpoints is exposed through parameter 42 delayed-data-transfer-supported (Boolean) under static-low-level-rx-endpoint. In case endpoint supports non-time 43 managed traffic - it is assumed that also time-managed traffic is supported by the endpoint (time-managed traffic support 44 is mandatory function whilst non-time managed traffic support is  optional function), the endpoint requires desired type 45

Further the 29 uplane-marking points to o-ran-interfaces.yang, where it ends up pointing to priority depending on actually used u-plane 30 transport (either PCP for Ethernet ot DCSP for IP). 12.4 Beamforming Configuration 11 The beamforming functionality allows the O-RU to influence the angle of the main lobe of the signal which is radiated 12 from/received by the O-RU. Beamforming support is optional and an O-RU shall indicate that it supports such 13 functionality by indicating that it supports the “urn:o-ran:beamforming:x.y” namespace. 14 A multi-band capable O-RU shall be able to support independent beamforming configuration on each of its supported tx-15 arrays and/or rx-arrays depends on O-RU antenna configuration. 16 12.4.1 Pre-Defined Beamforming Configuration 17 In case the O-RU supports beamforming, the o-ran-beamforming.yang and o-ran-uplane-conf,yang modules are used to 18 report the pre-defined relationship between supported beams to a NETCONF client. A band-number and/or capabilities-19 group is used to uniquely identify separate tx-arrays and/or rx-arrays supported by an O-RU with the beamforming 20 configuration referencing the set of tx-arrays and rx-arrays that are associated with this band and/or capabilities-group. 21

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        92
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 A default service area of the O-RU is determined as the grid of pre-defined beams. When O-RU updates beamforming 1 configuration as described in 12.4.2, the grid of pre-defined beams can be newly defined. In this case, the default service 2 area is changed accordingly.  3 O-RU may support new service area by applying tilt-offset to the given default service area in elevation and/or azimuth 4 domains as described in 12.4.3. 5 12.4.2 Beamforming Configuration Update 6 This section provides the method to modify and to apply the beamforming configuration (weights, attributes and/or beam 7 properties). The modification of the beamforming information is allowed only if O-RU supports the feature “MODIFY-8 BF-CONFIG” used for defining the modification of beamforming configuration. 9 The beamforming configuration is stored in the O-RU and comes from the O-RU’s software, treated in Chapter 5. The 10 O-RU shall locate the beamforming configuration file in the generic folder, i.e., O-RAN/beamforming/.  11 To modify the beamforming configuration, the following steps are applied. 12 1. NETCONF client can retrieve the file list of the O-RU’s folder: O-RAN/beamforming/. 13 2. NETCONF client can trigger the upload of the beamforming configuration file from the O-RU’s folder. 14 3. Operator can recover the uploaded file and edit the beamforming configuration file offline. 15 4. NETCONF client can download the file to the original folder. 16 The modified beamforming configuration file shall not have the same name as any other file in the folder. Its file name is 17 the matter of implementation.  18 The beam properties in -ran-beamforming YANG module contain coarse-fine, coarse-fine-beam-relation and 19 neighbor-beam for each beam-id. This information is received from the O-RU as O-RU's capability at O-RU start-up 20 and typically are used by the scheduler in O-DU. A NETCONF client (O-DU or NMS) can modify the beamforming 21 information via file described in this section. When the beamforming configuration (weight, attribute and beam properties) 22 is modified via file, the configuration of the beam properties list in the o-ran-beamforming YANG module should be 23 modified together via the same file if affected by the modified weight and/or attribute.  24 An O-RU supporting the modification of beamforming configuration shall support the storage of at least two beamforming 25 files per simultaneous band-number and/or capabilities-group supported. For each band within a multi-band O-RU or 26 each capabilities-group, one file corresponds to the pre-defined (factory, read-only) beamforming configuration and at 27 least one file corresponds to a modified (read-write) beamforming file. The O-RU has the responsibility to remove existing 28 file and prepares space for new file when the NETCONF client file-download rpc is issued. When the O-RU only supports 29 the storage of a single modified (read-write) beamforming file per band of operation, i.e., number-of-writable-30 beamforming-files = 1 the file-download operation for the modified beamforming configuration needs to be done while 31 neither tx-array-carriers nor rx-array-carriers are configured in the O-RU to avoid the removal of the modified 32 beamforming configuration file for the current active software.  33 If the O-RU supports the capability to store two or more modified beamforming configuration files per band of operation 34 in the O-RU, i.e., number-of-writable-beamforming-files > 1, the NETCONF file-download operation can be 35 performed without any timing limitation. That's because the modified beamforming configuration file for the current 36 beamforming configuration can be kept during the file-download operation. To apply the new modified beamforming 37 configuration, the following steps are applied: 38 1. The NETCONF client can download the file to the beamforming folder if the O-RU supports the capability number-39 of-writable-beamforming-files > 1. 40 2. The NETCONF client shall deactivate tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers in the U-Plane configuration by 41 setting "INACTIVE" for the active parameters, if they are ACTIVE. 42 3. Optionally, the NETCONF client shall delete tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers, if O-RU doesn't support the 43 capability update-bf-non-delete. 44 4. Alternatively, the NETCONF client can trigger the download of the modified beamforming configuration file to the 45 folder if the O-RU's capability is number-of-writable-beamforming-files =1. 46

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        93
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 5. The NETCONF client shall activate the modified beamforming configuration by using: 1 • activate-beamforming-config rpc and selecting the modified beamforming configuration file and the band-2 number for which this modified configuration applies, 3 • activate-beamforming-config-by-capability-group rpc and selecting the modified beamforming 4 configuration file and the capabilities-group for which this modified configuration applies. 5 6. If a NETCONF client subscribes to the notification beamforming-information-update and/or capability-group-6 beamforming-information-update in advance, the O-RU sends such notification to the subscribed NETCONF 7 client. Then the NETCONF client can subsequently retrieve beam properties in o-ran-beamforming YANG module 8 via NETCONF <get> operation. 9 7. Optionally, the NETCONF client shall create tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers again, if the O-RU doesn't 10 support the capability update-bf-non-delete. 11 8. The NETCONF Client shall activate tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers in the U-Plane configuration by 12 setting “ACTIVE” for active parameters. 13 Then the new edited beamforming information is applied to the new tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers in the U-14 Plane configuration. 15 [Abnormal handling] If the O-RU fails to activate the edited beamforming configuration file correctly, i.e., rpc error for 16 rpc activate-beamforming-config or activate-beamforming-config-by-capability-group, the O-RU shall revert back 17 to the pre-defined/factory beamforming configuration file and report this to the NETCONF client. 18 At the reset rpc, the beamforming configuration information is switched to the pre-defined beamforming configuration. 19 Even though the reset operation is issued, the O-RU may store the modified beamforming configuration file in the folder, 20 which is not used, if O-RU supports the capability persistent-bf-files to store them in the reset-persistent memory. 21 The file format of the beamforming configuration is O-RU implementation specific. 22   23 The diagrams below show two methods to modify the file of beamforming configuration information plus the method 24 how to apply the modified file for beamforming configuration conformation to use. 25

12.4.3 Tilting Pre-defined Beams 1 This section describes the optional capability by which the O-RU’s pre-defined beams may be tilted by using the 2 “BEAM-TILT” feature defined in the o-ran-beamforming YANG model. This capability is an O-RU specific 3 functionality, enabling adaptation of the service area associated with an O-RU without the need for operation of 4 additional ALDs described in Chapter 11, or modifying the beamforming configuration using the “MODIFY-BF-5 CONFIG” feature described in sub-section 12.4.2. 6  7 Note, the operation of the feature “BEAM-TILT” is independent to the operation of the “MODIFY-BF-8 CONFIG”. When the “MODIFY-BF-CONFIG” feature is used to define a new default service area, the 9 “BEAM-TILT” feature may be used to apply tilt-offsets to the newly defined service area.  10  11 O-RU can change the service area by applying a tilt-offset to the elevation and/or azimuth pointing angles for the pre-12 defined beams. This feature allows to shift beam characteristic of all predefined-beams in elevation and/or azimuth 13 direction (i.e. changing the service area or sector coverage) while preserving the beam adjacency among the beams within 14 grid of beams.  15 Note, elevation-tilt-offset-angle values smaller than 0 represents an up-shift of the default service area towards 16 the zenith (i.e., corresponding to a decrease in zenith angle) and values larger than 0 represent a down-shift of the 17 default service area away from the zenith (i.e., corresponding to an increase in zenith angle). 18 To shift service area of the O-RU in a different direction, O-RU controller shall check whether the O-RU supports feature 19 BEAM-TILT feature during capabilities negotiation of the NETCONF session. In the case that O-RU supports the 20 BEAM-TILT feature, at least one of the elevation-tilt-offset-granularity and azimuth-tilt-offset-granularity will be 21 read as greater than zero value from O-RU. Tilting is a per capabilities-group operation and hence the parameters are 22 defined per capabilities-group. If O-RU supports BEAM-TILT feature, O-RU controller can configure the values of 23 elevation-tilt-offset-angle and/or azimuth-tilt-offset-angle the configuration values should meet the ranges and 24 granularity information retrieved from predefined-beam-tilt-offset-information. 25
 26 Figure 50: Sequence diagram for predefined-beam-tilt-offset-information 27  28 Depending on O-RU’s implementation, the O-RU may need some time to complete the change of service area according 29 to the updated elevation-tilt-offset-angle and/or azimuth-tilt-offset-angle for a particular capabilities-group. The O-30 RU shall report its capability via the parameter, run-time-tilt-offset-supported. For O-RU with run-time-tilt-offset-31 supported = FALSE, changing the values in elevation-tilt-offset-angle and/or azimuth-tilt-offset-angle for a specific 32 capabilities-group shall be allowed only if all tx-array-carriers/rx-array-carriers corresponding to the capabilities-33

Copyright © 2019 by the O-RAN Alliance.  Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        96
ORAN-WG4.MP.0-v02.00.00 group is INACTIVE. When the service area change is completed in O-RU, the O-RU delivers the notification predefined-1 beam-tilt-offset-complete to inform the O-RU Controller which then may request to activate tx-array-carriers/rx-2 array-carriers in O-RU. For O-RU with run-time-tilt-offset-supported = TRUE, neither changing the state of tx-array-3 carriers/rx-array-carriers nor delivering notification predefined-beam-tilt-offset-complete is not required. 4
